  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d15f1b9d-ea53-4b6c-ac43-849b931618f8'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer9348986050617069312">In 1959, Jean Craighead George published <i>My Side of the Mountain</i>. This coming-of-age story about a boy and his falcon went on to win a Newbery Honor, and for the past forty years has enthralled and entertained generations of would-be Sam Gribleys. The two books that followed--<i>On the Far Side of the Mountain</i> and <i>Frightful's Mountain</i>--were equally extraordinary. Now all thre</span>
  <span id="freeText9348986050617069312" style="display:none">In 1959, Jean Craighead George published <i>My Side of the Mountain</i>. This coming-of-age story about a boy and his falcon went on to win a Newbery Honor, and for the past forty years has enthralled and entertained generations of would-be Sam Gribleys. The two books that followed--<i>On the Far Side of the Mountain</i> and <i>Frightful's Mountain</i>--were equally extraordinary. Now all three books are available in one deluxe yet affordable volume for veteran devotees and brand-new fans alike.</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/48272594-morgan"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/48272594-morgan">Morgan</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would highly reconmend this book. This book is about a boy who lives in the city with his family. He had a grandpa that owned a mountain back in the<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would highly reconmend this book. This book is about a boy who lives in the city with his family. He had a grandpa that owned a mountain back in the day. The boys dad had always talked about it. The boy never liked the city he wanted to run away to the mountain. The dad and him had always joked about the boy running away there. He really wated to. so one day he did. The dad thought that he wouldn run away then come back in a little bit, but the boy didnt. He actually went and found the mountain. He found a hollow tree and lived there. He made a few friends there... Animal friends. He lived there for a few years. One day his family decided to go look for him. They found him and had a bunch of reporters there to. The family wasnt worried at all they new he was safe. The family ended up making a wooden house there. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_34428044" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34428044" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1563888-james"><img alt="James" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34428044?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/1563888-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34428044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3692002949225505545"><br/>	My Side of the Mountain was an excellent book. I felt like I could relate to it so much. It’s about a boy who runs away from home and goes to live in the Catskill Mountains. He has heard stories of an old family member who used to live in these mountains. My favorite character is Sam Gribley, the boy who has run away. I feel like I am him in real life, I want to run away and live in the mountains somewhere. I don’t have a least favorite character, but I do have another favorite, Frightful. Frig</span>
  <span id="freeText3692002949225505545" style="display:none"><br />	My Side of the Mountain was an excellent book. I felt like I could relate to it so much. It’s about a boy who runs away from home and goes to live in the Catskill Mountains. He has heard stories of an old family member who used to live in these mountains. My favorite character is Sam Gribley, the boy who has run away. I feel like I am him in real life, I want to run away and live in the mountains somewhere. I don’t have a least favorite character, but I do have another favorite, Frightful. Frightful is a falcon that Sam took from a nest and raised himself. Sam has taught her to hunt for smaller animals, such as rabbits, squirrels, birds, even some snakes.<br />	I could never stop reading this book. Every line on every page kept me reading. I would recommend this book to people who love the wilderness, and an adventure. I wish they would make a movie for this movie. I think I would play the part of Sam Gribley, the wilderness boy. I just feel like I relate to him so much. Everything he does I would do, hunt, fish, build a house out of a tree. Jean Craighead has truly written the perfect. If you haven’t read this book, I strongly recommend you do. You will be entertained throughout the whole book. The story only gets better in the sequel. Sam’s sister joins him and something happens to his beloved falcon. The trilogy is more about frightful perspective on the mountain. How she has to hunt for Sam and live with him. I think it was a good idea to have the last book more about frightful, you learn more about her. It was great book and I recommend it for all. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3692002949225505545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17115472851600791661">Imagine- Leaving your home for an entire year, to live off the land. In the realistic fiction book, My Side of The Mountain, by Jean Craighead George, that's exactly what the main character Sam Gribley does. <br/><br/>Sam is a 12 year old teenage boy from New York City. His father had always told him about his grandfathers land, and Sam knew it was time to go find it, and leave the loud, packed, and stressful city. Over his year long journey, Sam encounters many different struggles, and other things in th</span>
  <span id="freeText17115472851600791661" style="display:none">Imagine- Leaving your home for an entire year, to live off the land. In the realistic fiction book, My Side of The Mountain, by Jean Craighead George, that's exactly what the main character Sam Gribley does. <br /><br />Sam is a 12 year old teenage boy from New York City. His father had always told him about his grandfathers land, and Sam knew it was time to go find it, and leave the loud, packed, and stressful city. Over his year long journey, Sam encounters many different struggles, and other things in the wilderness, and meets several new people along the way. I believe Sams message was always live life to the fullest, but to a certain extent. (Page ix in Author's Preference)"I packed my suitcase and told my mother I was going to run away form home. As I envisioned it, I would live by a waterfall in the woods and catch fish on hooks made from forks of tree limbs as I has been taught by my father."<br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone in a teenage age group, is very adventurous, and likes extremely realistic fiction. I give this book an overall rating of 4.5 stars out of 5 because it could include a bit more detail and description in some parts, but otherwise it was a significant novel. </span>

          </span>

I thought that it was really boring and that not much happened in the whole 177 pages of this book. I felt like the author just got bored with this book half way through and just wanted to finish this book. <br /><br />“My Side of the Mountain” starts off as him just surviving in the wilderness with his pet falcon named Fightfull. When he is in town he makes some friends and his friends tell there friends about him and then the word gets out that there is a boy living in the wilderness all by himself. That gets all over the news and his parents end up seeing it on the news. His parents go to rescue him and bring him but he does not want to go home. He ends up getting his parents to let him stay in the wilderness. His parents build him a cabin in the woods and they let him be free. <br /><br />I would not recommend this book to anyone. <div id="review_2126126303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2126126303" />
    <a title="Annika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68555400-annika"><img alt="Annika" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2126126303?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annika" href="/user/show/68555400-annika">Annika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2126126303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11662496551258998536">"My Side of the Mountain" by Jean Craighead George, is an extraordinary book about a young man, Sam Gribley, who leaves his cramped family home in New York City, to survive off of the family land in the Catskill Mountains. The book itself is written as if it is Sam's journal and is in first person point of view,and is a record of all of the things that Sam goes through as a result of surviving off of the land. <br/><br/>This story if one of my personal favorites due to the fact that it is about survival a</span>
  <span id="freeText11662496551258998536" style="display:none">"My Side of the Mountain" by Jean Craighead George, is an extraordinary book about a young man, Sam Gribley, who leaves his cramped family home in New York City, to survive off of the family land in the Catskill Mountains. The book itself is written as if it is Sam's journal and is in first person point of view,and is a record of all of the things that Sam goes through as a result of surviving off of the land. <br /><br />This story if one of my personal favorites due to the fact that it is about survival and nature, not from an adults point of view, but from a young person's point of view; apart from that it is an easy read that also contains really detailed drawings which are actually Sam's "diagrams" of what he is doing or seeing. One thing that I also find very interesting about the book is the fact that it creates a very beautiful relationship between Sam and his little companion, Frightful, a falcon that he took from a nest and raised from a young chic. This relationship is one of the most important aspects of the story because it is a driving force behind Sam's success and ability to survive through the difficulties of living off of the land. This also leads into one of my favorite parts of the book.<br /><br />There are two different parts in the book that I absolutely love, one of them being how Sam ends up with a falcon companion. I won't go into much detail, however I will say this, I enjoyed how it wasn't something randomly put into the book and actually was linked into the story, and I also found the way that he went about retrieving Frightful very funny and unique. My second favorite part of this narrative is the end and the twist that occurs, which happens to be a very sweet heart-warming addition to the story. I love how the author made sure there were no loose ends in the story by the way he connected everything at the end. It was one of those "Awwww!" moments that put a smile on my face.<br /><br />One thing that I wish would have been different is if the author made the transitions between one event to another a little smoother. I understand that the book is written as a series of journal entries, however, in between some of the events that take place there seems to be an almost abrupt pause that some what bothered me. Other than that, this was an amazing book that really captured my attention and made it nearly impossible to put down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11662496551258998536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="TJ  Beaver" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12708995-tj-beaver"><img alt="TJ  Beaver" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398957791p2/12708995.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/512833158?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TJ  Beaver" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TJ  Beaver" href="/user/show/12708995-tj-beaver">TJ  Beaver</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12708995-tj-beaver?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer512833158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5487262533736954153">My Side of the Mountain is a great historical fiction book. This book is about a young boy named Sam who hates his life in New York City and decides to come out to the Catskill Mountains and lives there. He chooses a big tree to live in and finds a little bird and trains her to hunt for him. Sam has to live off the gird, fend for himself, and survive. My favorite part of this book is when Sam gets his bird Frightful who was living in a nest as a little baby. Sam finds her as a baby and takes her</span>
  <span id="freeText5487262533736954153" style="display:none">My Side of the Mountain is a great historical fiction book. This book is about a young boy named Sam who hates his life in New York City and decides to come out to the Catskill Mountains and lives there. He chooses a big tree to live in and finds a little bird and trains her to hunt for him. Sam has to live off the gird, fend for himself, and survive. My favorite part of this book is when Sam gets his bird Frightful who was living in a nest as a little baby. Sam finds her as a baby and takes her back to train. This is my favorite part because I liked hearing about how cute frightful was as a baby. The author wrote this book because she loved how to describe being free. This was a truly free feeling book.<br /><br />I connected with Sam because there are some things I don't like in my life but unlike Sam I could never run away. I learned that worrying about things will never be any fun unless you try it, just like Sam tried so many different things and survived. For example Sam watches the animals to see what they eat so he knows what is edible. I would recommend this book to anybody who loves books because it is a short read but a great story. Overall I loved this book because it showed me the freeness to have fun. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348345057" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/849066-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591845271p2/849066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348345057?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/849066-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348345057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7819751937378266414">One of my favorite books as a kid was My Side of the Mountain and I just recently became aware of the fact that it had been turned into a trilogy. So I reread My Side of the Mountain and read Far Side of the Mountain and Frightful's Mountain. <br/><br/>I'm happy that a reread My Side because there were big chunks of the plot that I had forgotten about and would have been lost if I had just jumped into Far Side. I still loved My Side, really enjoyed Far Side, but didn't like Frightful's Mountain at all. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText7819751937378266414" style="display:none">One of my favorite books as a kid was My Side of the Mountain and I just recently became aware of the fact that it had been turned into a trilogy. So I reread My Side of the Mountain and read Far Side of the Mountain and Frightful's Mountain. <br /><br />I'm happy that a reread My Side because there were big chunks of the plot that I had forgotten about and would have been lost if I had just jumped into Far Side. I still loved My Side, really enjoyed Far Side, but didn't like Frightful's Mountain at all. The second book in this series is about Sam's life with his sister who has joined him on the mountain and about poaching. It held my interest and enjoyed learning more of their survival skills. The third book was from Frightful's perspective and I just don't enjoy hearing an animal's perspective....I think it's cheesy. Plus there was an environmental agenda throughout the whole book that I felt was shoved down my throat. My suggestion if you want to read all three is to read the first two and then read just the last few chapters of Frightful's Mountain so you can see how everything ends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7819751937378266414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Once I finish this, I know I will be reading it to my nephews and nieces, I trust it will spark that quest for knowledge and adventure that it did in me and countless other children.</span>

<div id="review_3488382135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3488382135" />
    <a title="John Geary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2325371-john-geary"><img alt="John Geary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449651365p2/2325371.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3488382135?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Geary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Geary" href="/user/show/2325371-john-geary">John Geary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3488382135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1362826823823301565">A series of adventures featuring Sam Gribley, a “modern-day” Huck Finn and his falcon, they’re written mainly as literature for children, with some adult themes (poaching, conservation) in them. Interesting book, or really, a series of books, as it is a trilogy of books written over a period of 40 years.<br/>That fact does create a few issues for me, in reading them back-to-back-to-back.<br/>The first book is set in 1959, the year it was published. The second book is set a year later, even though it was p</span>
  <span id="freeText1362826823823301565" style="display:none">A series of adventures featuring Sam Gribley, a “modern-day” Huck Finn and his falcon, they’re written mainly as literature for children, with some adult themes (poaching, conservation) in them. Interesting book, or really, a series of books, as it is a trilogy of books written over a period of 40 years.<br />That fact does create a few issues for me, in reading them back-to-back-to-back.<br />The first book is set in 1959, the year it was published. The second book is set a year later, even though it was published in 1990. The third book is a bit of a conundrum for me. Initially, it’s told from the point of view of the falcon, starting from almost the same point in time as the second book; it switches to the POV of Sam, then back to the birds again. I kind of liked that. But at one point in the book, one of the characters mentions he has a cellphone. Now the third story was published in 1999 – but it’s set in the early 1960s – NO ONE had cellphones then. That type of sloppy plotting drives me to distraction. I realize it was written in a way that if you had not read the first book, you might get away with it. However, there’s an inconsistency in that children in the book are writing snailmail letters, not email. Very poor continuity.<br />I realize it’s children’s lit; but as a child, I would have found that glaring error just as irritating. I wonder if the writer (now deceased) actually did NOT write that part in, perhaps an overzealous editor inserted it? Because it’s completely unnecessary for the development of the story, so why even include it when it sticks out like such a big sore thumb?<br />By and large, I enjoyed the books for what they were. But that one point really drops it from a 4 to a 3.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1362826823823301565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2728786033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11385796694991481728">My Side of the Mountain is a thrilling story for all ages! It taps the spirit of adventure and the search for the unknown in all of us. It's a book of challenges, of failures...and eventually successes. Miss George developed her main character, Sam, in such a way as to bring the reader along on his journey into the forest of his ancestors and his attempt, in a very natural way, to share the land with Frightful, his pet falcon.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3216932420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17693760306012510737">I really enjoyed the book. Usually i'd read a harder book but this book was worthwhile. I really like the part when he created his shelter in a tree. He sort of reminds me also of myself because I try as much as I can to challenge myself at some sort of survival. Like for I think three days my mom was mad with me so I cooked all my meals myself. It was successful and luckily I didn't starve to death.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3425468989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3425468989" />
    <a title="Cindy Stavropoulos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65568420-cindy-stavropoulos"><img alt="Cindy Stavropoulos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488548468p2/65568420.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy Stavropoulos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy Stavropoulos" href="/user/show/65568420-cindy-stavropoulos">Cindy Stavropoulos</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3425468989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8110535389491044223">I read this book as a kid! It really did have a profound affect on my life and the desire to be in nature. I haven’t hollowed a tree and moved to the mountains but I do regularly hike and backpack. As an adult, each word feels the same as when I was a kid. I find it very interesting how he survives and the ways he survives. What a great story, even the second time around. I bought a used hard copy for my grandchildren to read!! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11455998-todd?shelf=children-s-books">children-s-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11455998-todd?shelf=manhood">manhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11455998-todd?shelf=classic">classic</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3627247148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1937157167382828103">I enjoyed reading this book for its light-hearted tale of a very resourceful and independent boy. It is far fetched especially in today's cultural context, but it was fun to imagine the kid accomplishing so much on his own and doing it out of enjoyment and not out of drudgery. It gives a few good opportunities for thoughtful reflection on topics like dependence versus independence, family, community, resourcefulness, and conservation.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8d6w2a2RvpTrPoIKAeLWRlGoB3y72jM9TAZPAQQpDZz/72qv45W/VSXeFVz6yA8kAIkLJvMqfCMPAs+9eBCwcg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mmw329wpxU3Zhuc+jDxnj9d1KQoAeuQX5Ax9/IPu4O+UXe2tki3EjBdmcGh3Fr7thlQlUEiKqwmnCP1A/9ddAQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9889863111034144911">Jean Craighead George wrote over eighty popular books for young adults, including the Newbery Medal-winning <i>Julie of the Wolves</i> and the Newbery Honor book <i>My Side of the Mountain</i>. Most of her books deal with topics related to the environment and the natural world. While she mostly wrote children's fiction, she also wrote at least two guides to cooking with wild foods, and an autobiography, <i>Journey</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9889863111034144911" style="display:none">Jean Craighead George wrote over eighty popular books for young adults, including the Newbery Medal-winning <i>Julie of the Wolves</i> and the Newbery Honor book <i>My Side of the Mountain</i>. Most of her books deal with topics related to the environment and the natural world. While she mostly wrote children's fiction, she also wrote at least two guides to cooking with wild foods, and an autobiography, <i>Journey Inward</i>.<br /><br />The mother of three children, (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/292093.Twig_C__George" title="Twig C. George" rel="nofollow noopener">Twig C. George</a>, Craig, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3244462.T__Luke_George" title="T. Luke George" rel="nofollow noopener">T. Luke George</a>) Jean George was a grandmother who joyfully read to her grandchildren since the time they were born. Over the years Jean George kept one hundred and seventy-three pets, not including dogs and cats, in her home in Chappaqua, New York. "Most of these wild animals depart in autumn when the sun changes their behaviour and they feel the urge to migrate or go off alone. While they are with us, however, they become characters in my books, articles, and stories."</span>

Young Sam Gribley gets to the end of the block and keeps going--all the way to the Catskill Mountains of upstate New York. There he sets up house in a huge hollowed-out tree, with a falcon and a weasel for companions and his wits as his tool for survival. In a spellbinding, touching, funny account, Sam learns to live off the land, and grows up a little in the process. Blizzards, hunters, loneliness, and fear all battle to drive Sam back to city life. But his desire for freedom, independence, and adventure is stronger. No reader will be immune to the compulsion to go right out and start whittling fishhooks and befriending raccoons.  Jean Craighead George, author of more than 80 children\'s books, including the Newbery Medal-winning Julie of the Wolves, created another prizewinner with My Side of the Mountain--a Newbery Honor Book, an ALA Notable Book, and a Hans Christian Andersen Award Honor Book. Astonishingly, she wrote its sequel, On the Far Side of the Mountain, 30 years later, and a decade after that penned the final book in the trilogy, Frightful\'s Mountain, told from the falcon\'s point of view. George has no doubt shaped generations of young readers with her outdoor adventures of the mind and spirit.
